increase dramatically\nas these missions\n\n15.1 INTRODUCTION\nThe SeaWiFS Project developed\nthe SeaWiFS\nBio-optical\nArchive\nand\nStorage\nSystem\n(SeaBASS)\nto be a local repository\nfor in situ\noptical and pigment data products regularly used in\na variety of scientific analyses.\nInformation\non the\noriginal\nSeaBASS\ndesign\nis provided\nin the\nSeaWiFS\nTechnical\nReport Series, (Hooker et al.\n1994).\nThe system has since been expanded\nto\ncontain data sets collected\nby participants\nof the\nSIMBIOS\nProject (NASA Research Announcement\n1996 and 1999).\nA detailed\ndescription\nof the\nSeaBASS\nsystem is available\nvia the World Wide\nWeb at http://seabass.gsfc.nasa.gov.\nBoth the SeaWiFS and SIMBIOS Projects use\nin situ bio-optical\ndata for the validation\nof\nSeaWiF-S _and other (e.g. OCTS, POLDER) satellite\ndata products,\nand for the development\nof new\nocean\nchlorophyll\nalgorithms.\nIn\naddition\nSeaBASS\nsupports\ninternational\nprotocol\nworkshops,\ndata merger studies, and time series\nstudies.\nArchived\ndata include measurements\nof\n\nbegin to require\n\nvalidation\n\n15.2 SeaBASS\n\ndata.\n\nDATA\n\nFORMAT\n\nSeaBASS presently contains over 10,000 biooptical data files, encompassing\nmore than 400\nseparate experiments.\nIn addition,\nits historical\npigment database\nholds over 300,000\nrecords of\nphytoplankton\npigment data.\nTo account for the\ncontinuous\ngrowth of the data archive, the Project\nbelieved\nit essential\nto develop\nefficient\ndata\ningestion and storage techniques.\nSuch ingestion\nprocedures\nand protocols\nwere designed to be as\nstraightforward\nand effortless\nas possible\non the\npart of the contributing\ninvestigators,\nwhile still\noffering a useful format for internal analysis efforts.\nThe Project considered the following to be the most\nimportant in-the design of the system:\n\nwater-leaving\nradiance,\nCh|orophyii-a,\nand other\nrelated\noptical\nand pigment\nparameters.\nWhen\navailable, additional\noceanographic\ndata (e.g. water\ntemperature,\nsalinity,\ntotal suspefided\nparticulate\nmatter (SPM),\nand chromatic\ndissolved\norganic\nmatter (CDOM) and atmospheric\ndata (e.g. aerosol\noptical\nthickness\n(AOT)\nare also archived\nin\nSeaBASS.\nData are collected\nby a number of\ndifferent\ninstrument\npackages,\nsuch as profilers,\nbuoys, and above-water\nmeasurement\ndevices, on a\nvariety of platforms, including ships, moorings, and\ndrifters.\nThe contents\nof SeaBASS\nare made\nreadily available to SIMBIOS and MODIS Science\nTeam Members\nand to other approved individuals\non a case by case basis (e.g. members of other\nocean\ncolor\ninstrument\nteams,\nvolunteercontributing\nresearchers,\netc.).\nAccess\nto the\ndatabase and data archive is available to authorized\n\n1.\n2.\n3.\n\nsimple data format, easily read and updated,\nglobal\nportability\nacross\nmultiple\ncomputer\nplatforms; and\nWeb accessible data holdings.\n\nAs a result, SeaBASS\nsupports standard,\nflat\n(two-dimensional)\nASCII\ntext files,\nwhich\nare\neasily managed from any computer platform and by\nmost programming\nlanguages.\nThe architecture\nof\na SeaBASS data file is simple: data are presented in\ncolumns (delimited\nby spaces, tabs, or commas)\nand preceded\nby a series of predefined\nmetadata\nheaders.\nThe\nheaders\nprovide\ndescriptive\ninformation\non the data file, such as date, time,\nlocation,\ninvestigators,\ncolumn\nnames and units,\n\nusers via the World Wide Web (WWW).\n\n17o\n\nOcean ptics rotocols\nO\nP\nForSatellite cean olor ensor\nO\nC Several 15.4 DATA QUALITY\na\nexamplesf SeaBASSatafiles are available\no\nd\nonline at: http:llseabass.gsfc.nasa.govlseabass\nTo assist with the standardization\nof\n_submit.html.\nAppendix provides detailed\nB\na\ndata files, the Project developed\nfeedback\ndescription\noftheSeaBASS\nfileformat.\n15.3 SeaBASS\n\nSeaBASS\nsoftware\nand protocols\nto evaluate the format of submitted\ndata files. The primary component of the software\nis known as FCHECK.\nFCHECK\nconsists\nof a\n\nARCHITECTURE\n\nPERL (Practical Extraction\nand Report Language)\nscript with connections\nto several look-up tables\nand\nUNIX\nmail\nhandling\nutilities.\nData\ncontributors,\nusing any computer platform, may test\na data file for compatibility\nwith the SeaBASS\nformat\nby electronically\nmailing\nthe\nfile\nto\nfcheck@seabass.gsfc.nasa.gov.\nUpon receipt of the\nfile, FCHECK\nparses the data and metadata\nand\ncompares\nit to the required\nSeaBASS\nformat.\nResults of this analysis are electronically\nmailed to\nthe contributor\nand to the SeaBASS Administrator.\n\nSeaBASS\ncontains\ntwo separate\nbut linked\nentities, a data archive and a relational database.\nThe data\narchive\nconsists\nof series\nof subdirectories organized by affiliation, experiment,\nand\ncruise.\nEach cruise has additional\nsubdirectories\ncontaining\nthe\nin situ\ndata\nsets,\nassociated\ndocumentation,\nand calibration files associated with\nthat cruise.\nAuthorized\nusers may peruse\nthe\ndirectory tree via the SeaBASS web page.\nPresently,\nthe database\nconsists\nof a single\ntable with numerous\ncolumns\nto store metadata\ninformation.\nEach row in the table contains the\nname of the data file and all of the header\n\nThis\nformat\nanalysis\nrequires\nlittle\nintervention\non behalf of the Administrator\n\nproven\nto reduce\nconsiderably\nthe amount\nof\nprocessing\ntime needed for both the Administrator\nand\ncontributor.\nAdditional\ninformation\non\nFCHECK\nis\navailable\nonline\nat\n\ninformation\nprovided in that file. Hence, data files\nmeeting\npre-defined\ncriteria may be located by\nperforming\nsimple\nkeyword\nsearches\non the\nmetadata.\nAuthorized\nusers\nmay search\nthe\ndatabase\nusing\nthe SeaBASS\nweb\nserver\nat\nhttp://seabass.gsfc.nasa.gov/dataordering.html\nThe web-based\ninterface\nallows (1) simple\nkeyword\nsearches\nof the headers\n\'affiliations\',\n\'investigators\',\n\'experiment\',\n\'cruise\', \'data_type\'\nand\n\'fields\', (2) the application\nof user defined date,\ntime,\nlatitude,\nand longitude\nranges,\nand (3)\nadvanced keyword searches of all of the metadata\ninformation\nvia a user-written\nquery.\nData files\nmeeting applied search conditions\nmay be viewed\nvia the World\nWide Web or compressed\nand\ndownloaded\nto an FI\'P (File Transfer Protocol) site.\nRedesign\nof the SeaBASS\ndatabase began in\nSpring 2000, and is expected to be operational\nin\nWinter 2000. Changes to the database will include:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nhttp://seabass.gsfc.nasa.gov/fcheck_desc.html.\nOnce\ndata are prepared\nfor archival,\nthe\ncontributor\nuploads the data files, calibration\nfiles,\nand supporting documentation\nto SeaBASS via File\nTransfer Protocol (FTP).\nThe Administrator\nthen\ncollects the files and evaluates\nthe data set. The\nfollowing requirements\nneed to be met:\n(1) data\nfiles must be organized\nin the proper SeaBASS\nformat (i.e. FCHECK\ndoes not report any errors),\n(2) supporting documentation\nand calibration\nfiles\nmust be included\nin the submission,\nand (3) the\ndocumentation\nand calibration\nfiles must match\nthose\nlisted\nin\nthe\n\'documents\'\nand\n\'calibration_files\'\nheaders in each data file.\nAdditionally,\nthe\ndocumentation\nand\ncalibration files are inspected for completeness.\nAt\na minimum, the Project requires that documentation\ninclude a cruise report or station log (with ancillary\ninformation\nsuch\nas\ndate,\ntime,\nlocation\ncoordinates,\nwater\ndepth,\nsea and sky states,\nobservations,\nand notes) and an instrument\nreport\n(with\ninformation\nsuch\nas instruments\nused,\nprocessing\nmethods,\nequations,\nand references).\nThe Project encourages\nthe contributor\nto include\nadditional\ndocumentation,\nsuch\nas\ndigital\nphotographs\nof sea and sky states. Calibration\nfiles\nmust include calibration\ncoefficients\nand the date\neach instrument was calibrated.\nOnce the data set\nhas passed\nvisual inspection,\nthe Administrator\narchives the data files and ingests the appropriate\ninformation\ninto the database.\nAt this point, the\n\nan increase in the number of tables to improve\ndata normalization\nand database performance,\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\na reconfiguration\nof the\nsystem\nto take\nadvantage\nof multiple computer processors\nand\nincreased physical storage space,\nthe\nutilization\nof\nstored\nprocedures\nand\napplications\nfor internal\nSIMBIOS\nProject\nOffice accounting activities, and\nthe ability to ingest bio-optical and pigment data\ninto tables within the database.\nThe latter will\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nto\nno\nand has\n\nallow specific data values to be extracted by\nperforming\nsimple\nkeyword\nsearches\non the\nmetadata\nor by applying range conditions (e.g.\nwaveband, depth, etc.) on the data tables.\n\n171\n\nOcean ptics rotocols\nO\nP\nForSatellite cean olor ensor\nO\nC S\nValidation\nnewdatabecomevailable\na\nonlineto theScience manuscript resulting from use of\nTeam.\ninitial submission\nfor publication,\n15.5 ACCESS\n\nPOLICY\n\nthe data prior to\nthus providing\nthe data provider an opportunity\nto comment on the\npaper. All users and providers are required to report\nto SeaBASS\nadministration\npossible data errors or\nmislabels found in the database.\n\nAND\n\nUSERS\n\nto\n\nThe policy applies to data submitted\nto the\nNASA SIMBIOS Project at GSFC for inclusion in\nthe calibration\nand validation\ndata collection.\nThis\n\nA major\nfacilitate\n\npurpose of the SeaBASS database is\ncomparisons\nbetween\nin\nsitu\n\nobservations\n(regionally,\ntemporally,\nby technique,\nby investigator,\netc.), as well as between in situ and\nremotely\nsensed\nobservations.\nUpdates\nand\ncorrections\nto submitted data sets are encouraged.\nRecords\nwill be maintained\nof updates\nand\ncorrections and a summary of new and updated data\nwill be posted\nonline.\nIt is the provider\'s\nresponsibility\nthat the current data in the archive\nwill be identical to the data used in the provider\'s\nmost recent publications\nor current research.\nAt the\nend of each SIMBIOS\ncontract,\na final data\nresubmission,\nor a written\ncertification\nof data\nquality, from the provider is mandatory.\nAfter receiving\nthe final data, the SIMBIOS\nProject will forward the data at the appropriate\ntime\nto NODC for open distribution.\nA courtesy citation,\nnaming the provider and the funding agency, will\naccompany\nthe data. The SIMBIOS Project will not\nbe held responsible\nfor any data errors or misuse.\nData copyright is retained by the US Government.\nTo afford continued\nrapid submission\nof data\nsets, the SeaBASS web server has been configured\nas a password protected\nsystem. Additionally,\nthe\nweb server and SeaBASS\nsoftware\nlog all user\nactivity.\nThis\ninformation\nis\navailable\nto\ncontributing\ninvestigators.\n\npolicy supercedes\nthe SeaWiFS Project 1991 policy\n(Appendix\nA in Hooker\net. ai.,\n1993).\nThe\nSIMBIOS\ninvestigators\nmust,\nat a minimum,\ncomply with SIMBIOS\ndata policy, although\nthe\nProject encourages\na more open policy.\nOcean color algorithm development\nis severely\nobservation\nlimited.\nAs such, rapid turnaround and\naccess to field data are essential to advance the state\nof the art. Data obtained under SIMBIOS NRA-99\ncontracts\nmust be submitted\nno later than six\nmonths from the date of collection.\nInternational\nSIMBIOS\nScience Team and researchers\ninvolved\nin other ocean color missions (i.e., POLDER, GLI,\nMODIS, MERIS,\netc.) are encouraged\nto provide\ntheir data as well, in order to foster collaboration.\nFor a period of three years following\ndata\ncollection,\naccess to the digital data will be limited\nto SIMBIOS\nScience\nTeam members\nand other\napproved\nusers as agreed upon by the SIMBIOS\nProject and data providers. The SIMBIOS\nProject\nwill grant access to the international\nscience team\nmembers\non a case by case basis according\nto\nongoing\ncollaboration\ntasks.\nOther investigators\nfrom the ocean color community\nwill be able to\nquery information\nabout the data (i.e., parameters,\nlocations, dates and investigators),\nbut will not have\naccess\nto the data itself.\nInstead,\nif they are\ninterested\nin the data, they will be referred to the\nprovider.\nAfter the third year anniversary\nof data\ncollection,\nthe data will change from a "restricted"\nto an "open" status and will be distributed\nby\nNational\nOceanographic\nData Center\n(NODC).\nSome special data sets for algorithm development\nwill be made available\nto the research community\nwithout\nrestrictions\nwith the approval\nof the\nSIMBIOS Science Team.\n\nREFERENCES\nHooker, S.B., C.R. Jeremy\nI Science\n\nWerdell\nSystem\n\n2Future\n3SAIC\n\nSeaBASS\n\nGeneral\n\nData File Format\n\n1, Sean\nand\n\nTech\n\nB\n\nBailey\n\n! and Giulietta\n\nApplications\n\nInc.,\n\nCorporation,\n\nSciences\n\nGreenbelt,\n\nCorporation,\n\napplicable)\nis assigned\nto any header\nwhere\ninformation\ncannot be provided.\nData files with\nmissing headers will not be accepted for submission\nto SeaBASS.\nA description of each follows.\n\'Data_file_name\'\nsimply provides the name of\nthe data file.\n\'Affiliations\',\n\'investigators\',\nand\n\'contact\'\nprovide information\non the contributing\nresearchers.\nThe primary investigator\nis listed first,\nfollowed by any associate investigators.\nCommas\nseparate\nmultiple\nentries,\nand white spaces\nand\napostrophes\nare not allowed.\n\'Contact\' is the\nelectronic\nmail\naddress\nof\nthe\ncontributor.\n\'Experiment\',\n\'cruise\',\nand\n\'station\'\nrecord\ninformation\non\nthe long-term\nexperiment\n(if\navailable), the specific cruise, and the station within\nthe cruise.\nFor each of the latter, an entry of\n\'SIMBIOS\'\nis not permitted.\n\'Documents\'\nrefers to\ncruise reports, logs, and associated\ndocumentation\nthat provide\nadditional\ninformation\nabout\nthe\nexperiment\nor cruise.\n\'Calibration_files\'\npoints to\nadditional\nfile(s) that contain the coefficients\nand\ntechniques used to calibrate the instruments used in\ndata\ncollection.\nThe\nfiles\nreferred\nto by\n\'documents\'\nand\n\'calibration_files\'\nmust\n\n3\n\nMaryland\n\nMaryland\n\nBeltsvilIe,\n\nfor vertical\n\nHEADERS\n\nEach header begins with a \'I\' and every data\nfile opens with \'begin_header\'.\nThe headers are\nthen listed in any order, as long as the list ends with\n\'end_header\'.\nA value of \'NA\' (not available\nor\n\nLanham,\n\nS. Fargion\n\nprofiles\n\nMaryland\n(e.g. optical\n\npackages,\n\nCTD);\n\n\'flow_thru\nfor continuous data (e.g. underway flow\nthrough systems); \'above_water\'\nfor above surface\nradiometry\ndata (e.g. ASD, SIMBAD);\n\'sunphoto\'\nfor sunphotometry\ndata (e.g. MicroTops,\nPREDE);\n\'mooring\'\nfor moored data and buoy data; \'drifter\'\nfor drifter\nand drogue data; \'scan\'\nfor discrete\nhyperspectral\nmeasurements\n(e.g.,\nabsorption\nspectra);\nand \'pigment\'\nfor laboratory\nmeasured\npigment\ndata\n(fluorometry,\nspectrophotometry,\nHPLC). \'North_latitude\',\n\'south_latitude\',\n\'east_long\nitue\',\n\'west_longitude\',\n\'start_date\',\nenddate\',\n\'start_time\',\nand \'end_time\'\nprovide information\non\nthe location,\ndate, and time data were collected.\nEach entry should be the extreme\nvalue for the\nentire data file. For example, \'north_latitude\'\nrefers\nto the coordinate furthest north data in the file were\ncollected.\n\'Start_time\'\nand \'end_time\'\nrefer to the\nearliest and latest time-of-day\ndata in the file were\ncollected.\nThe latter do not refer to the time data\ncollection\nbegan\nand\ndata\ncollection\nceased,\nrespectively.\nLatitude and longitude\nare listed in\ndecimal\ndegrees,\nwith coordinates\nnorth of the\nequator or east of the Prime Meridian set positive\nand south of the equator\nor west of the Prime\nMeridian\nset negative.\nDates have the format\n\'YYYYMMDD\'.\nTimes\nhave\nthe\nformat\n\'HH:MM:SS\'\nand are listed in Greenwich\nMean\nTime (GMT).\n\'Cloud_percent\',\n\'wave_height\',\n\'wind_speed\',\n\'secchi_depth",\n\'measurement_depth\',\nand\n\'water_depth\'\nprovide ancillary\ninformation\nabout\nthe station,\nwhen available.\n\'Wave_height\'\nand\n\'water_depth\'\nhave\nunits\nof\nmeters\nand\n\naccompany the data files at the time of submission.\n\'Data_status\'\ndescribes\nthe condition\nof the\ndata file, accepting\nvalues of preliminary,\nupdate,\nand final.\n\'Preliminary\'\nis used when the data are\nsubmitted\nfor the first time and the investigator\nintends\nto analyze\nthe data further.\n\'Update\'\nindicates\nthe data\nare being\nresubmitted\nand\ninforms the Project that an additional resubmission\nwill occur in the future.\n\'Final\' is used when the\ninvestigator\nhas no intention of revisiting the data\nset.\n\'Data_type\'\ndescribes\nthe general collection\nmethod of the data. Accepted values include: \'cast\'\n\n\'wind_speed\'\nhas units of meters per second.\nA\nvalue for \'measurement_depth\'\nis included when the\nfile contain data collected at a discrete depth (e.g.,\nbottle samples or buoy/moored\nradiometers).\n\'Fields\' names each of the columns of in situ\ndata presented\nbelow the headers.\nEach entry\ndescribes\nthe data in a one column,\nand every\ncolumn must have an entry.\n\'Units\' provides the\nunits for each column\nof data.\nEvery value in\n\'fields\'\nmust also have an equivalent\nentry in\n\n176\n\nOcean ptics rotocols\nO\nP\nForSatellite\nOcean olor ensor\nC S\nValidation\nof\nv\n\'units\'.\'Missing\'\nrefers a null value\nto\nused\nasa development the expandedersionof the\nplaceholder\nforanymissing ata\nd point. ABSTRACT\n\n(Maximum\n\n200 words)\n\nThe document stipulates protocols for measuring bio-opticai and radiometric data for the Sensor\nlntercomparison\nand Merger for Biological and Interdisciplinary\nOceanic Studies (SIMBIOS) Project activities\nand algorithm development. This document supersedes the earlier version (Mueller and Austin 1995) published\nas Volume 25 in the SeaWiFS Technical Report Series. This document marks a significant departure from, and\nimprovement on, theformat and content of Mueller and Austin (1995). The authorship of the protocols has been\ngreatly broadened to include experts specializing in some key areas. New chapters have been added to provide\ndetailed and comprehensive\nprotocols for stability monitoring of radiometers using portable sources, abovewater measurements\nof remote-sensing\nreflectance, spectral absorption measurements\nfor discrete water\nsamples, HPLC pigment analysis and fluorometric pigment analysis. Protocols were included in Mueller and\nAustin (1995) for each of these areas, but the new treatment makes significant advances in each topic area.\nThere are also new chapters prescribing protocols for calibration of sun photometers and sky radiance sensors,\nsun photometer and sky radiance measurements\nand analysis, and data archival. These topic areas were barely\nmentioned in Mueller and Austin (1995).\n14. SUBJECT\n\nSeaWiFS,\n\nTERMS\n\nSIMBIOS,\n\n15. NUMBER\n\nocean\n\noptics,\n\nocean\n\ncolor\n\nsensor\n\n_16. PRICE\n\n17. SECURITY\nCLASSIFICATION18. SECURITY\nCLASSIFICATION 19. SECURITY CLASSIFICATION\nOFREPORT\nOFTHISPAGE\nOF ABSTRACT\nUnclassified\nUnclassified\nUnclassified\nNSN 7540-01-280-5500\n\nOF PAGES\n\n184\n\nvalidation.\n\nCODE\n\ni|\n\n20. LIMITATION\n\nOF ABSTRACT\n\nUL\nStandard\nPrescribed\n\nForm\nby ANSI\n\n298\nStd.\n\nfReT.\nZ39.tB\n\n2-89)\n\n'
